class="om ff on ny nz oo op bf b bg z du">Photo By <a class="af oq" href="https://unsplash.com/ko/@diesektion?utm_content=creditCopyText&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_source=unsplash" rel="noopener rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Unsplash</a></figcaption></figure><h1 id="ef01" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Executive Summary</h1><ul class=""><li id="caa3" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">In December 2023, S2W’s threat intelligence center(a.k.a. Talon) discovered and continuously tracked the Rust-based macOS malware named <strong class="my gv">RustDoor</strong> (a reference to the name given by <a class="af oq" href="https://www.bitdefender.com/blog/labs/new-macos-backdoor-written-in-rust-shows-possible-link-with-windows-ransomware-group/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">BitDefender</a>) disguised as a VisualStudio update.</li><li id="9ebf" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Through further analysis, we identified the Windows version of RustDoor, which we named <strong class="my gv">GateDoor</strong> because it was written in Golang rather than Rust.</li><li id="1f7a" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Both RustDoor and GateDoor have been confirmed to be distributed under the guise of normal program updates or utilities, and in particular, RustDoor uses Apple-related keywords such as <em class="nx">Mac</em>, <em class="nx">iCloud</em>, and <em class="nx">Apple</em> as the address of the C&amp;C server.<br/> — Additional cases of distribution through job search themes were also discovered.</li><li id="023f" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">GateDoor was distributed by disguising itself as the <em class="nx">WebViewHost</em> utility and using the DLL Search Order Hijacking(T1574.001) technique to load a malicious DLL that downloads GateDoor.</li><li id="d6d1" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Both malware receive and execute commands from the C&amp;C server and perform malicious actions such as collecting information, downloading additional files, and executing commands.<br/> — RustDoor focuses on backdoor functions, but GateDoor has many loader functions.</li><li id="af97" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">(<strong class="my gv">Similarity</strong>) RustDoor and GateDoor have overlapping endpoints used when communicating with the C&amp;C server and have similar functions, <br/>so the same attacker developed them.</li><li id="9681" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">The infrastructure used by the two malware appears to be <strong class="my gv">related to a RaaS affiliate</strong> called <strong class="my gv">ShadowSyndicate</strong>, and the possibility that they are cybercrime collaborators who specialize in providing infrastructure cannot be ruled out.</li></ul><h1 id="3bc4" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Introduction</h1><p id="c58b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">Recently, a lot of malware targeting macOS users has been discovered. <a class="af oq" href="https://www.jamf.com/blog/jtl-malware-pirated-applications/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">ZuRu malware variant</a> and <a class="af oq" href="https://www.sentinelone.com/blog/backdoor-activator-malware-running-rife-through-torrents-of-macos-apps/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">macOS.Bkdr.Activator</a>, which were distributed in pirated macOS applications are such cases.</p><p id="929c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">On this background, attackers’ use of Golang and Rust, which support cross-platforms, is increasing, and the possibility of writing code more efficiently by utilizing AI technologies such as chatGPT and Copilot when developing malware <a class="af oq" href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/security/blog/2024/02/14/staying-ahead-of-threat-actors-in-the-age-of-ai/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">has undoubtedly increased</a>. It is also worth noting that attackers are putting a lot of effort into attacking the macOS environment as the number of MacBook users has increased since the introduction of Apple’s silicon chip. So, malware targeting macOS does malicious acts such as stealing information stored in macOS or secretly using device resources.</p><p id="717b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">In December 2023, Talon, the threat research center in S2W, discovered that macOS malware named <strong class="my gv">RustDoor</strong> (a reference to the name from <a class="af oq" href="https://www.bitdefender.com/blog/labs/new-macos-backdoor-written-in-rust-shows-possible-link-with-windows-ransomware-group/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">BitDefender</a>) disguised as a VisualStudio update is being distributed. At the time of discovery, not a single one was detected as malicious based on VirusTotal, which shows that malicious macOS target binaries written in Rust are more difficult to detect than Windows in current security products. This report covers a detailed analysis of the identified RustDoor malware and introduces Windows-targeting malware identified as the predecessor of RustDoor.</p><h1 id="95ca" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Attack Overview</h1><p id="9417" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">We have identified the following key characteristics after tracking RustDoor malware over the past 3 months. S2W internally named the malware family <strong class="my gv">GateDoor</strong>, but to distinguish it from BitDefender’s RustDoor, the macOS version will be called RustDoor, and the Windows malware version will be called GateDoor.</p><h2 id="fccb" class="qc os gu bf ot qd qe dy ox qf qg ea pb nh qh qi qj nl qk ql qm np qn qo qp qq bk">1. Cross Platform</h2><p id="ae53" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">The initial version of RustDoor is believed to have been produced based on Golang for the Windows environment and was developed at least before the end of September 2023. Afterward, the attacker targeted macOS and developed malware based on Rust, and it is believed that preparations for the attack were completed at least in December 2023. It is expected that the attacker developed the malware in Golang and Rust, with various environments in mind from the early stages of malware development. Additionally, it is expected that during this process, it was produced in Golang and then changed to Rust, which is more difficult to analyze. The macOS version of RustDoor targets Silicon MacBooks. Among the hunted RustDoor files, many file names start with <em class="nx">localfile~</em> because each ARM and Intel binary in one RustDoor binary was separated and submitted to VirusTotal. <br/>(Silicon binaries include binaries for both ARM and Intel versions.)</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div du">Figure 1. RustDoor malware reported in VirusTotal</figcaption></figure><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz qs"><picture><source srcSet="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:640/format:webp/1*JIE5Vti3wkiJLw6Iia0d8w.png 640w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:720/format:webp/1*JIE5Vti3wkiJLw6Iia0d8w.png Filenames of RustDoor and GateDoor</figcaption></figure><h2 id="f884" class="qc os gu bf ot qd qe dy ox qf qg ea pb nh qh qi qj nl qk ql qm np qn qo qp qq bk">2. Disguising as a legitimate file</h2><p id="3041" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">RustDoor is disguised as a normal update program, as it is distributed under file names such as <strong class="my gv">VisualStudioUpdater</strong> and <strong class="my gv">ChromeUpdates</strong>. <br/>In addition to file names, some specific words were used in distribution sites and C&amp;C servers. In particular, keywords such as “<em class="nx">Mac</em>,” “<em class="nx">iCloud</em>,” and “<em class="nx">Apple</em>” related to Apple were used as the address of the C&amp;C server.</p><p id="1278" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">It was confirmed that the GateDoor was distributed disguised as a normal <em class="nx">WebViewHost</em> utility. At the time, since it was distributed to Windows, general keywords were used in the domain address.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh The infrastructure of RustDoor and GateDoor</figcaption></figure><h2 id="cdbb" class="qc os gu bf ot qd qe dy ox qf qg ea pb nh qh qi qj nl qk ql qm np qn qo qp qq bk">3. Initial stages</h2><p id="17e8" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">GateDoor and RustDoor seem to be distributed by encouraging people to download utilities or fake normal update programs through distribution sites disguised as normal. However, it has also been found that RustDoor was distributed under the guise of a job search theme.</p><p id="f243" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">GateDoor</strong></p><p id="aef3" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">GateDoor was distributed disguised as a utility called <em class="nx">WebViewHost</em>. The attacker distributed the legitimate <em class="nx">WebViewHost</em> utility in the form of a ZIP file or MSI file, and by applying the <em class="nx">DLL Search Order Hijacking</em> technique when the user runs the WebViewHost.exe file, the malicious WebView2Loader.dll file is loaded. After that, the DLL file downloads and executes the GateDoor malware from an external server. As confirmed, the <strong class="my gv">edging.zip</strong> file was used in late September, and the <strong class="my gv">BinMS.msi</strong> file was used in early November 2023. In the case of MSI files, files are created in the path below when executed.</p><ul class=""><li id="a6b2" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">C:\Users\[Username]\AppData\Roaming\MicrosoftEdging</li></ul><p id="5305" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The GateDoor Downloader contains the following config values, and these values are encrypted with a specific XOR key value (“nfmMoPCj”).<br/> — GateDoor download base URL<br/> — GateDoor download URL path<br/> — File name saved locally after downloading<br/> — HKEY_CURRENT_USER\ActivateS sub registry key value (<em class="nx">MicrosoftEdging</em>)</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz The infection process of GateDoor</figcaption></figure><p id="3b2e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">In addition, the distribution method via MSI files discovered in early November 2023 included the MSI file, GateDoor Downloader, and GateDoor malware signed with a valid certificate.</p><ul class=""><li id="480e" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Singer: AAAA CLEANING REMOVALS LIMITED</li><li id="2d43" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Serial: 22 CA CB 0C F8 24 EE B9 3E 3B 1B AA 77 99 0E 28</li><li id="243c" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Date signed: 2023–10–27 UTC</li></ul><p id="f866" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">RustDoor — Job search theme</strong></p><p id="1a56" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">In one case, it was found that RustDoor malware was distributed disguised as a job-related file. A shell script file that downloads RustDoor and normal document files was distributed with the file name <em class="nx">Jobinfo.app.zip</em>, and when the script file is executed, RustDoor malware is Information on RustDoor Infrastructure</figcaption></figure><p id="ba00" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The attacker initially built infrastructure through hosting companies in Eastern Europe, such as Russia and Romania. In particular, the Romanian IP (193.29.13.152) was used as a C&amp;C server and domain registration site. When distributing malware, they avoided using IPs, created domains, and used various hosting servers worldwide. In this respect, there is a possibility that the attacker is geopolitically located in Eastern Europe.</p><h1 id="9eb6" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Detailed Analysis</h1><p id="bdfa" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">This chapter provides a detailed analysis of the RustDoor malware. This file is malware written in Rust, targets macOS, and can attack both Intel and Apple Silicon chipsets.</p><h2 id="473e" class="qc os gu bf ot qd qe dy ox qf qg ea pb nh qh qi qj nl qk ql qm np qn qo qp qq bk">1. RustDoor v1</h2><p id="22bd" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">In the case of the early version of RustDoor, no separate configuration information exists internally. The early version of RustDoor registers malware in the macOS startup program by creating a new plist in the /Library/LaunchAgents path to maintain persistence.</p><p id="3935" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><em class="nx">| Table 7. Content of the plist</em></p><pre class="ob oc od oe of qv qw qx bp qy bb bk"><span id="a87d" class="qz os gu qw b bg ra rb l rc rd">&lt;?xml version=&quot;1.0&quot; encoding=&quot;UTF-8&quot;?&gt;<br/>&lt;!DOCTYPE plist PUBLIC &quot;-//Apple//DTD PLIST 1.0//EN&quot; &quot;http://www.apple.com/DTDs/PropertyList-1.0.dtd&quot;&gt;<br/>&lt;plist version=&quot;1.0&quot;&gt;<br/>&lt;dict&gt;<br/> &lt;key&gt;Label&lt;/key&gt;<br/> &lt;string&gt;com.apple.visualstudio&lt;/string&gt;<br/> &lt;key&gt;Program&lt;/key&gt;<br/> &lt;string&gt;{Path to RustDoor}&lt;/string&gt;<br/> &lt;key&gt;KeepAlive&lt;/key&gt;<br/> &lt;dict&gt;<br/>  &lt;key&gt;SuccessfulExit&lt;/key&gt;<br/>  &lt;false/&gt;<br/> &lt;/dict&gt;<br/> &lt;key&gt;RunAtLoad&lt;/key&gt;<br/> &lt;true/&gt;<br/>&lt;/dict&gt;<br/>&lt;/plist&gt;</span></pre><h2 id="cf0f" class="qc os gu bf ot qd qe dy ox qf qg ea pb nh qh qi qj nl qk ql qm np qn qo qp qq bk">2. RustDoor v2</h2><p id="399a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">RustDoor v2, later updated, stores configuration information in JSON format within the malware to support various persistence methods depending on the situation. RustDoor reads the value immediately after execution and determines how to maintain persistence for each field.</p><p id="4c30" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><em class="nx">| Table 8. Configuration in RustDoor</em></p><pre class="ob oc od oe of qv qw qx bp qy bb bk"><span id="674f" class="qz os gu qw b bg ra rb l rc rd">{<br/>  &quot;daemonize&quot;: true,<br/>  &quot;check_cron_asked&quot;: true,<br/>  &quot;lock_in_cron&quot;: true,<br/>  &quot;lock_in_dock&quot;: true,<br/>  &quot;lock_in_launch&quot;: false,<br/>  &quot;copy_files&quot;: true,<br/>  &quot;apps&quot;: [ { &quot;id&quot;: 1,<br/>                  &quot;name&quot;: &quot;Firefox&quot;,<br/>                  &quot;path&quot;: &quot;/Applications/Firefox.app/&quot;,<br/>                  &quot;icon&quot;: &quot;/Applications/Firefox.app/Contents/Resources/firefox.icns&quot;,<br/>                  &quot;exec&quot;: &quot;firefox&quot;,<br/>                  &quot;show_dialog&quot;: false,<br/>                  &quot;dialog_title&quot;: &quot;title&quot;<br/>                 }, … <br/><br/></span></pre><p id="a3f4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The setting values that confirm the function in the above settings are as follows.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div Role of each field in the configuration</figcaption></figure><h2 id="e2da" class="qc os gu bf ot qd qe dy ox qf qg ea pb nh qh qi qj nl qk ql qm np qn qo qp qq bk">3. Common malicious behavior</h2><h2 id="760f" class="qc os gu bf ot qd qe dy ox qf qg ea pb nh qh qi qj nl qk ql qm np qn qo qp qq bk">3.1 Register</h2><ul class=""><li id="dc11" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">/gateway/register</li></ul><p id="2a67" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">RustDoor transmits information about the infected device to the C&amp;C server through an HTTP POST request and receives the client’s unique ID from the server. The URL used here is <strong class="my gv"><em class="nx">[Base C2 URL]/gateway/register</em></strong> and the data below is delivered in JSON format.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz The information delivered for the register</figcaption></figure><p id="092a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Only a number is received as a response value without any other format; that number is the client ID given to the infected device.</p><h2 id="d733" class="qc os gu bf ot qd qe dy ox qf qg ea pb nh qh qi qj nl qk ql qm np qn qo qp qq bk">3.2 Malicious Action</h2><ul class=""><li id="9920" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">/gateway/report</li></ul><p id="96fd" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">RustDoor periodically requests commands from the C&amp;C server every second. Command requests are made to <strong class="my gv"><em class="nx">[Base C2 URL]/gateway/report</em></strong> and the assigned client ID is delivered in JSON format.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og Delivery of command results</figcaption></figure><h2 id="97aa" class="qc os gu bf ot qd qe dy ox qf qg ea pb nh qh qi qj nl qk ql qm np qn qo qp qq bk">4. GateDoor</h2><p id="0956" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">GateDoor, designed to <strong class="my gv">target the Windows</strong> operating system with <strong class="my gv">endpoints and</strong> <strong class="my gv">protocols similar to RustDoor</strong>, was additionally identified. The malware is written in Golang and is focused on executing arbitrary code or executable files in various ways.</p><ul class=""><li id="fff3" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Filename: Algols.dll</li><li id="1a92" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">MD5: a73d8e923452bfb1c752aa5adea287b7</li><li id="deb7" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">SHA256: 9dd66e5692e496c9cfcc647edf593c323404424cad61276725efb934b64b96e9</li></ul><h2 id="b4ae" class="qc os gu bf ot qd qe dy ox qf qg ea pb nh qh qi qj nl qk ql qm np qn qo qp qq bk">4.1 Commonalities with future_task, a separate endpoint used only by GateDoor, has been additionally confirmed.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj GateDoor implements various methods to maintain persistence, but internal fixed values determine the method.</p><blockquote class="nu nv nw"><p id="b0b4" class="mw mx nx my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Note that the installation path of legitimate EXE file that loads the GateDoor downloader is <strong class="my gv">C:\Users\[username]\AppData\Roaming\MicrosoftEdging\WebViewHost.exe.</strong></p></blockquote><ol class=""><li id="3786" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt rx pv pw bk">Register the EXE path into C:\ProgramData\Microsoft\Windows\Start Menu\Programs\Startup</li><li id="b6a7" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt rx pv pw bk">Register into the run registry to run GateDoor when boot-up<br/> — Path: SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run<br/>— Key: MicrosoftOffice.Hub<br/>— Value: [The EXE path]</li></ol><p id="e9b4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">3. Utilize schtasks.exe<br/>— schtasks.exe /Create /SC ONLOGON /F /TN MicrosoftEdging /TR [The EXE path]<br/>— schtask.exe /Create /SC onidle /F /TN MicrosoftEdging /TR [The EXE path] /i 30</p><p id="b6cb" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The command request through the <em class="nx">gateway/report</em> endpoint is the same, but the response value has an added field called <strong class="my gv">exe_param</strong>, which is an argument required for file execution in addition to the argument for the command.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz rh"><picture><source List of command</figcaption></figure><h2 id="1421" class="qc os gu bf ot qd qe dy ox qf qg ea pb nh qh qi qj nl qk ql qm np qn qo qp qq bk">5. DataCollector</h2><p id="ce10" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">Additional malware was identified that communicated with the <strong class="my gv">sarkerrentacars[.]com</strong> domain. It is equally written in Golang and uses the internal name DataCollector. DataCollector has commands to collect information on infected devices targeting Intel macOS devices and sending the output results to the command attacker’s server using the GET method. The commands that DataCollector executes to collect data are as follows. As a result, the stolen information includes system information, network information, software information, hardware information, registered daemon list, kernel parameter list, and disk information.</p><p id="e3e8" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><em class="nx">| Table 20. List of commands that DataCollector executes</em></p><pre class="ob oc od oe of qv qw qx bp qy bb bk"><span id="bf9c" class="qz os gu qw b bg ra rb l rc rd">system_profiler SPSoftwareDataType SPHardwareDataType<br/>networksetup -listallnetworkservices<br/>networksetup -listallhardwareports<br/>launchctl list<br/>sysctl -a<br/>diskutil list</span></pre><h1 id="f5aa" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Attribution</h1><p id="9109" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">In September 2023, Group-IB unveiled a new RaaS (Ransomware-as-a-Service) Affiliate called <strong class="my gv">ShadowSyndicate</strong>. They identified 85 servers <strong class="my gv">using the same SSH Fingerprint</strong> <strong class="my gv">key</strong> from July 16, 2022, to September 2023, and these servers were used as C&amp;C servers for malware such as Cobalt Strike, IcedID, and Sliver. Since these servers have been identified to be related to 7 ransomware groups, it is presumed that the group is an affiliate collaborating with several RaaS groups.</p><ul class=""><li id="df24" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Reference: <a class="af oq" href="https://www.group-ib.com/blog/shadowsyndicate-raas/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Dusting for fingerprints: ShadowSyndicate, a new RaaS player?</a></li></ul><p id="eb4d" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">While tracking the infrastructure of the RustDoor malware, we found a correlation between the IP of the C&amp;C server (193.29.13[.]167, 88.214.26[.]22) and <strong class="my gv">ShadowSyndicate</strong>. As a result of pivoting the SSH Fingerprint key released by Group-IB, the 193.29.13[.]167 IP was discovered. Since the Issuer &amp; JARM of the SSL certificate used by 193.29.13[.]167 and 88.214.26[.]22 are the same, the infrastructure is also suspected of being related to ShadowSyndicate. This information was already made known on X by <a class="af oq" href="https://twitter.com/TLP_R3D/status/1718317301672333669" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Chris Duggan</a>.</p><ul class=""><li id="241b" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">SSH Fingerprint: Association with ShadowSyndicate (Source: <a class="af oq" href="https://twitter.com/TLP_R3D/status/1718317301672333669" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">X</a>)</figcaption></figure><p id="9563" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">We additionally traced the infrastructure of the GateDoor malware we identified. In this process, we discovered that many servers used the same SSH Fingerprint value as the IP(193.29.13[.]152) assigned to the C&amp;C server domain (trendfilesalgol[.]com). As a result of investigating the servers, they were used as C&amp;C servers for various malware such as Cobalt Strike, StealC, and TrueBot, and the watermark of Coblat Strike Beacon was the same as that mentioned by Group-IB. Among these, the watermark used by Clop (<strong class="my gv">1580103824</strong>) and the Watermark used by ALPHV and Nokoyawa (<strong class="my gv">674054486</strong>) were identified.</p><ul du">Figure 8. Part of the IPs mentioned by Joshuapenny<br/>(Source: <a class="af oq" href="https://osintteam.blog/infrastructure-analysis-lockbit-3-0-799a4ff1ca59" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Infrastructure Analysis: LockBit 3.0 Ransomware Affiliates Exploit CVE 2023–4966 Citrix Bleed Vulnerability</a>)</figcaption></figure><p id="64b6" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Given that the above infrastructures are heavily linked to cybercriminals such as RaaS, we estimate that cybercriminals, not the APT group, are behind this malware. As previously disclosed by <a class="af oq" href="https://twitter.com/TLP_R3D/status/1718317301672333669" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Chris Duggan</a>, there is a connection with the ShadowSyndicate threat actor. This is supported by the fact that the method of distributing malware and the features of the malware are not yet sophisticated and that it is different from existing APT groups. However, given that the infrastructure identified as ShadowSyndicate is very extensive and many cyber-criminals are connected, we should consider the possibility of a cybercrime collaborator specializing in providing infrastructure.</p><h1 id="29b7" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Conclusion</h1><ul class=""><li id="4b9f" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">In December 2023, RustDoor, a new type of malware targeting macOS, was discovered, and S2W has been tracking the malware and attack group for the past three months.</li><li id="2247" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Circumstances were discovered that GateDoor, the Windows version of RustDoor, was distributed first in September 2023, at least two months ago, and the two malware are evaluated to have been produced by the same creator.</li><li id="4c19" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">However, RustDoor performs the role of a backdoor, and GateDoor commands are focused on the role of a loader that loads additional malicious code.</li><li id="53c4" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">The infrastructure used by the two malware appears to be related to a RaaS group affiliate called ShadowSyndicate, and the possibility that they are cybercrime collaborators who specialize in providing infrastructure cannot be ruled out.</li><li id="e75d" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Given that many features and obfuscation techniques have not been applied, both RustDoor and GateDoor are expected to be in the early stages of development, and features may continue to be added in the future.</li></ul><h1 id="122d" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Appendix A.
